### [1] [Lost in Translation: How Language Re-Aligns Vision for Cross-Species Pathology](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04405)
*Ekansh Arora*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They study why vision–language pathology FMs struggle across cancers and species, diagnose an embedding/semantic collapse problem, and show that aligning visual features to language "anchors" mitigates it and improves AUC, though still short of SOTA in cross-species transfer.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Cross-cancer and cross-species generalization of pathology foundation models is unclear. Prototype-based or naïve vision–language alignments may overfit to species/tissue domains, failing to capture conserved tumor semantics. The authors seek to quantify these failures and introduce a mechanism to stabilize semantics across domains.

Method: Evaluate CPath-CLIP on canine and human WSI patches under same-cancer, cross-cancer, and cross-species transfer; few-shot fine-tuning; measure AUC; analyze embeddings (cosine similarity of tumor/normal prototypes), Grad-CAM attention; benchmark against H-optimus-0; propose "Semantic Anchoring" to align visual features to language-derived coordinates; run ablations isolating text-alignment effects from text-encoder complexity.

Result: Few-shot tuning increases AUC in same-cancer (64.9→72.6) and cross-cancer (56.84→66.31). Cross-species transfer via tissue matching works but lags H-optimus-0 (84.97 AUC). Embedding analysis shows >0.99 cosine similarity between tumor/normal prototypes (collapse). Grad-CAM: prototype models remain domain-locked; language-guided models focus on conserved tumor morphology. Semantic Anchoring yields additional gains (+8.52 same-cancer, +5.67 cross-cancer) independent of text-encoder size and avoids collapse observed in CPath-CLIP.

Conclusion: Standard vision–language alignment is insufficient for cross-species generalization due to species-dominated semantic collapse. Language-driven anchoring can act as a control signal to re-interpret visual features and improve transfer without retraining, partially closing the gap to SOTA but not yet matching it.

Abstract: Foundation models are increasingly applied to computational pathology, yet their behavior under cross-cancer and cross-species transfer remains unspecified. This study investigated how fine-tuning CPath-CLIP affects cancer detection under same-cancer, cross-cancer, and cross-species conditions using whole-slide image patches from canine and human histopathology. Performance was measured using area under the receiver operating characteristic curve (AUC). Few-shot fine-tuning improved same-cancer (64.9% to 72.6% AUC) and cross-cancer performance (56.84% to 66.31% AUC). Cross-species evaluation revealed that while tissue matching enables meaningful transfer, performance remains below state-of-the-art benchmarks (H-optimus-0: 84.97% AUC), indicating that standard vision-language alignment is suboptimal for cross-species generalization. Embedding space analysis revealed extremely high cosine similarity (greater than 0.99) between tumor and normal prototypes. Grad-CAM shows prototype-based models remain domain-locked, while language-guided models attend to conserved tumor morphology. To address this, we introduce Semantic Anchoring, which uses language to provide a stable coordinate system for visual features. Ablation studies reveal that benefits stem from the text-alignment mechanism itself, regardless of text encoder complexity. Benchmarking against H-optimus-0 shows that CPath-CLIP's failure stems from intrinsic embedding collapse, which text alignment effectively circumvents. Additional gains were observed in same-cancer (8.52%) and cross-cancer classification (5.67%). We identified a previously uncharacterized failure mode: semantic collapse driven by species-dominated alignment rather than missing visual information. These results demonstrate that language acts as a control mechanism, enabling semantic re-interpretation without retraining.

</details>


### [2] [Recognition of Daily Activities through Multi-Modal Deep Learning: A Video, Pose, and Object-Aware Approach for Ambient Assisted Living](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04509)
*Kooshan Hashemifard,Pau Climent-Pérez,Francisco Florez-Revuelta*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Multi-modal ADL recognition for Ambient Assisted Living: fuses 3D CNN video features, 3D human-pose GCN, and object-context via cross-attention; shows competitive accuracy on Toyota SmartHome.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Enable reliable in-home monitoring and support for older adults, despite challenges like intra-class variability, inter-class similarity, environmental changes, viewpoint shifts, and scene clutter in indoor settings.

Method: A three-branch pipeline: (1) visual stream with a 3D CNN for spatiotemporal cues; (2) skeletal stream with a Graph Convolutional Network on 3D human poses; (3) object detection to extract contextual cues. Cross-attention fuses object context with 3D CNN features; outputs are combined for activity classification.

Result: On the Toyota SmartHome dataset of real-world indoor activities, the approach attains competitive classification accuracy across varied daily activities (no explicit numbers provided).

Conclusion: The fusion of visual, pose, and contextual information improves robustness of ADL recognition and is promising for AAL applications that aim to enhance safety and autonomy of older adults.

Abstract: Recognition of daily activities is a critical element for effective Ambient Assisted Living (AAL) systems, particularly to monitor the well-being and support the independence of older adults in indoor environments. However, developing robust activity recognition systems faces significant challenges, including intra-class variability, inter-class similarity, environmental variability, camera perspectives, and scene complexity. This paper presents a multi-modal approach for the recognition of activities of daily living tailored for older adults within AAL settings. The proposed system integrates visual information processed by a 3D Convolutional Neural Network (CNN) with 3D human pose data analyzed by a Graph Convolutional Network. Contextual information, derived from an object detection module, is fused with the 3D CNN features using a cross-attention mechanism to enhance recognition accuracy. This method is evaluated using the Toyota SmartHome dataset, which consists of real-world indoor activities. The results indicate that the proposed system achieves competitive classification accuracy for a range of daily activities, highlighting its potential as an essential component for advanced AAL monitoring solutions. This advancement supports the broader goal of developing intelligent systems that promote safety and autonomy among older adults.

</details>


### [3] [InverseNet: Benchmarking Operator Mismatch and Calibration Across Compressive Imaging Modalities](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04538)
*Chengshuai Yang,Xin Yuan*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They introduce InverseNet, a cross-modality benchmark to quantify and study operator mismatch in compressive imaging (CASSI, CACTI, single-pixel cameras). Deep learning methods collapse (10–21 dB loss) under realistic mismatch, but operator-conditioned models plus simple blind calibration can recover most of the lost performance, with trends validated on real hardware.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Operator mismatch between the assumed forward model and the true physical system is ubiquitous in deployed compressive imagers yet unbenchmarked. A small deviation (eight parameters) can erase SOTA performance (e.g., EfficientSCI loses 20.58 dB). The field needs a standardized way to measure robustness and the effectiveness of calibration.

Method: Build a cross-modality benchmark (InverseNet) spanning CASSI, CACTI, and single-pixel cameras. Define a four-scenario protocol—ideal, mismatched, oracle-corrected, and blind calibration—and evaluate 12 reconstruction methods over 27 simulated scenes and 9 real captures. Compare mask-oblivious vs operator-conditioned architectures and quantify robustness, including correlation analyses.

Result: (1) Deep learning methods lose 10–21 dB under mismatch, negating their edge over classical baselines. (2) Across modalities, performance and robustness are inversely correlated (Spearman r_s = -0.71, p < 0.01). (3) Mask-oblivious networks recover 0% of mismatch losses regardless of calibration; operator-conditioned methods recover 41–90%. (4) Simple blind grid-search calibration recovers 85–100% of the oracle bound without ground truth. (5) Hardware experiments mirror simulation results.

Conclusion: Operator mismatch is a primary failure mode for modern compressive imaging reconstructions. Benchmarks should report robustness under mismatch. Architectures that ingest operator information and incorporate blind calibration are markedly more reliable, while classical methods remain competitive when mismatch is present. The provided benchmark and code aim to standardize evaluation and drive development of robust, operator-aware models.

Abstract: State-of-the-art EfficientSCI loses 20.58 dB when its assumed forward operator deviates from physical reality in just eight parameters, yet no existing benchmark quantifies operator mismatch, the default condition in deployed compressive imaging systems. We introduce InverseNet, the first cross-modality benchmark for operator mismatch, spanning CASSI, CACTI, and single-pixel cameras. Evaluating 12 methods under a four-scenario protocol (ideal, mismatched, oracle-corrected, blind calibration) across 27 simulated scenes and 9 real hardware captures, we find: (1) deep learning methods lose 10-21 dB under mismatch, eliminating their advantage over classical baselines; (2) performance and robustness are inversely correlated across modalities (Spearman r_s = -0.71, p < 0.01); (3) mask-oblivious architectures recover 0% of mismatch losses regardless of calibration quality, while operator-conditioned methods recover 41-90%; (4) blind grid-search calibration recovers 85-100% of the oracle bound without ground truth. Real hardware experiments confirm that simulation trends transfer to physical data. Code will be released upon acceptance.

</details>


### [4] [Fusion and Grouping Strategies in Deep Learning for Local Climate Zone Classification of Multimodal Remote Sensing Data](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04562)
*Ancymol Thomas,Jaya Sreevalsan-Nair*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Systematic study of multimodal fusion for LCZ classification (SAR+MSI) finds a simple hybrid feature-level fusion, enhanced by band grouping and label merging, delivers the best accuracy (76.6%) and benefits rare classes.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Urban climate analysis needs accurate Local Climate Zone (LCZ) maps. Multimodal remote sensing (SAR+MSI) can help, but deep learning fusion choices (pixel/feature/decision levels, attention, multi-scale) lack a comprehensive, controlled comparison—especially regarding underrepresented LCZ classes.

Method: Evaluate CNN-based multimodal fusion variants on So2Sat LCZ42: (i) baseline hybrid feature-level fusion (FM1), (ii) fusion with self-/cross-attention (FM2), (iii) multi-scale Gaussian filtered images (FM3), (iv) weighted decision-level fusion (FM4). Perform ablations across pixel-, feature-, and decision-level fusions. Study grouping strategies: band grouping within modalities and label merging in ground truth. Assess impact on overall and minority-class performance; release code and processed data.

Result: FM1 consistently outperforms simpler baselines; FM1 combined with band grouping (BG) and label merging (LM) yields the best overall accuracy of 76.6%. Strategies notably improve prediction for underrepresented classes. Code and datasets are released.

Conclusion: Thoughtfully designed hybrid feature fusion, augmented by data-aware band grouping and selective label merging, is more effective than attention-based or multi-scale add-ons for LCZ classification on So2Sat LCZ42. Fusion design and class/grouping strategy are key levers for boosting accuracy, especially for rare classes.

Abstract: Local Climate Zones (LCZs) give a zoning map to study urban structures and land use and analyze the impact of urbanization on local climate. Multimodal remote sensing enables LCZ classification, for which data fusion is significant for improving accuracy owing to the data complexity. However, there is a gap in a comprehensive analysis of the fusion mechanisms used in their deep learning (DL) classifier architectures. This study analyzes different fusion strategies in the multi-class LCZ classification models for multimodal data and grouping strategies based on inherent data characteristics. The different models involving Convolutional Neural Networks (CNNs) include: (i) baseline hybrid fusion (FM1), (ii) with self- and cross-attention mechanisms (FM2), (iii) with the multi-scale Gaussian filtered images (FM3), and (iv) weighted decision-level fusion (FM4). Ablation experiments are conducted to study the pixel-, feature-, and decision-level fusion effects in the model performance. Grouping strategies include band grouping (BG) within the data modalities and label merging (LM) in the ground truth. Our analysis is exclusively done on the So2Sat LCZ42 dataset, which consists of Synthetic Aperture Radar (SAR) and Multispectral Imaging (MSI) image pairs. Our results show that FM1 consistently outperforms simple fusion methods. FM1 with BG and LM is found to be the most effective approach among all fusion strategies, giving an overall accuracy of 76.6\%. Importantly, our study highlights the effect of these strategies in improving prediction accuracy for the underrepresented classes. Our code and processed datasets are available at https://github.com/GVCL/LCZC-MultiModalHybridFusion

</details>


### [5] [Structure-Guided Histopathology Synthesis via Dual-LoRA Diffusion](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04565)
*Xuan Xu,Prateek Prasanna*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Dual-LoRA Controllable Diffusion unifies histopathology local completion and global synthesis in one centroid-guided diffusion model, using multi-class nuclei centroids as strong, lightweight priors and two LoRA adapters to specialize tasks, yielding markedly better fidelity and realism than SOTA baselines.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Restoration and generation are often treated as separate problems despite sharing the goal of structure-consistent tissue synthesis under varying image missingness; existing methods rely on weak or inconsistent structural priors, leading to unrealistic cellular organization. A unified approach with stronger, annotation-efficient priors is needed.

Method: A controllable diffusion framework conditioned on multi-class nuclei centroids as spatial priors. Two task-specific LoRA adapters (for local completion and global synthesis) specialize a shared diffusion backbone, avoiding separate model training and enabling guidance under both partial and full image absence.

Result: Consistent gains over GAN and diffusion baselines. For local completion, masked-region LPIPS improves from 0.1797 (HARP) to 0.1524. For global synthesis, FID improves from 225.15 (CoSys) to 76.04, indicating better structural fidelity and realism.

Conclusion: The method provides more faithful structural recovery in masked areas and substantially improved realism and morphology consistency for full-image synthesis, enabling scalable, pan-cancer histopathology modeling within a single, controllable diffusion framework.

Abstract: Histopathology image synthesis plays an important role in tissue restoration, data augmentation, and modeling of tumor microenvironments. However, existing generative methods typically address restoration and generation as separate tasks, although both share the same objective of structure-consistent tissue synthesis under varying degrees of missingness, and often rely on weak or inconsistent structural priors that limit realistic cellular organization.
  We propose Dual-LoRA Controllable Diffusion, a unified centroid-guided diffusion framework that jointly supports Local Structure Completion and Global Structure Synthesis within a single model. Multi-class nuclei centroids serve as lightweight and annotation-efficient spatial priors, providing biologically meaningful guidance under both partial and complete image absence. Two task-specific LoRA adapters specialize the shared backbone for local and global objectives without retraining separate diffusion models. Extensive experiments demonstrate consistent improvements over state-of-the-art GAN and diffusion baselines across restoration and synthesis tasks.
  For local completion, LPIPS computed within the masked region improves from 0.1797 (HARP) to 0.1524, and for global synthesis, FID improves from 225.15 (CoSys) to 76.04, indicating improved structural fidelity and realism. Our approach achieves more faithful structural recovery in masked regions and substantially improved realism and morphology consistency in full synthesis, supporting scalable pan-cancer histopathology modeling.

</details>


### [6] [Mask-aware inference with State-Space Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04568)
*Ignasi Mas,Ramon Morros,Javier-Ruiz Hidalgo,Ivan Huerta*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Introduces Partial Vision Mamba (PVM), a mask-aware variant of Mamba/SSM blocks that handles arbitrarily shaped invalid inputs, showing benefits on depth completion, inpainting, and classification with missing data.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Partial Convolutions solved irregular missing-data handling for CNNs, but modern State Space Models (SSMs) like Mamba lack an equivalent inference-time mechanism; many vision tasks face irregular masks, so SSMs need a principled way to ignore/renormalize invalid pixels.

Method: Port the principles of partial operations to Mamba by incorporating mask-aware normalization/gating into the vision Mamba backbone (PVM) and provide rules for designing architectures with PVM, aiming to preserve linear-time efficiency while conditioning updates only on valid inputs.

Result: Across depth completion, image inpainting, and classification with invalid data, PVM is reported to be effective and generalizable; the abstract implies consistent robustness/performance gains, though no quantitative metrics are provided here.

Conclusion: PVM enables SSM-based vision models to robustly process inputs with arbitrarily shaped missing regions, extending the utility of Mamba to real-world scenarios with invalid data and offering a plug-and-play design framework.

Abstract: Many real-world computer vision tasks, such as depth completion, must handle inputs with arbitrarily shaped regions of missing or invalid data. For Convolutional Neural Networks (CNNs), Partial Convolutions solved this by a mask-aware re-normalization conditioned only on valid pixels. Recently, State Space Models (SSMs) like Mamba have emerged, offering high performance with linear complexity. However, these architectures lack an inherent mechanism for handling such arbitrarily shaped invalid data at inference time. To bridge this gap, we introduce Partial Vision Mamba (PVM), a novel architectural component that ports the principles of partial operations to the Mamba backbone. We also define a series of rules to design architectures using PVM. We show the efficacy and generalizability of our approach in the tasks of depth completion, image inpainting, and classification with invalid data.

</details>


### [7] [PinPoint: Evaluation of Composed Image Retrieval with Explicit Negatives, Multi-Image Queries, and Paraphrase Testing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04598)
*Rohan Mahadev,Joyce Yuan,Patrick Poirson,David Xue,Hao-Yu Wu,Dmitry Kislyuk*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: PinPoint is a new, large-scale benchmark for composed image retrieval that adds multiple correct answers, hard negatives, paraphrase robustness, multi-image composition, and demographic metadata, revealing major gaps in current methods and offering an MLLM-based training-free reranker to mitigate them.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing CIR benchmarks use single ground-truth labels and lack annotations to assess false-positive avoidance, robustness to instruction paraphrases, multi-image reasoning, and fairness—hindering realistic evaluation and progress.

Method: Construct the PinPoint benchmark: 7,635 real-world queries, 329K relevance judgments, 23 categories; provide ~9.1 correct answers per query, explicit hard negatives, six paraphrases per query, support for multi-image compositions (13.4% of queries), and demographic metadata. Evaluate 20+ methods across four paradigms and introduce a training-free reranking step leveraging an off-the-shelf multimodal LLM that can sit atop any CIR system.

Result: State-of-the-art models reach only 28.5% mAP@10, retrieve hard negatives ~9% of the time, and show 25.1% variance across paraphrases; performance on multi-image queries drops by 40–70% across methods. The proposed MLLM-based reranker helps close these gaps (qualitatively indicated; exact gains not specified in the abstract).

Conclusion: PinPoint exposes key weaknesses in CIR—false-positive sensitivity, paraphrase brittleness, and multi-image reasoning deficits—while offering a comprehensive benchmark and a practical, training-free reranking approach. All images, queries, annotations, index, and benchmarking code are released to catalyze research and fair evaluation.

Abstract: Composed Image Retrieval (CIR) has made significant progress, yet current benchmarks are limited to single ground-truth answers and lack the annotations needed to evaluate false positive avoidance, robustness and multi-image reasoning. We present PinPoint, a comprehensive real world benchmark with 7,635 queries and 329K relevance judgments across 23 query categories. PinPoint advances the field by providing: (1) multiple correct answers (averaging 9.1 per query) (2) explicit hard negatives, (3) six instruction paraphrases per query for robustness testing, (4) multi-image composition support (13.4% of queries), and (5) demographic metadata for fairness evaluation. Based on our analysis of 20+ methods across 4 different major paradigms, we uncover three significant drawbacks: The best methods while achieving mAP@10 of 28.5%, still retrieves irrelevant results (hard negatives) 9% of the time. The best models also exhibit 25.1% performance variation across paraphrases, indicating significant potential for enhancing current CIR techniques. Multi-image queries performs 40 to 70% worse across different methods. To overcome these new issues uncovered by our evaluation framework, we propose a training-free reranking method based on an off-the-shelf MLLM that can be applied to any existing system to bridge the gap. We release the complete dataset, including all images, queries, annotations, retrieval index, and benchmarking code.

</details>


### [8] [SGR3 Model: Scene Graph Retrieval-Reasoning Model in 3D](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04614)
*Zirui Wang,Ruiping Liu,Yufan Chen,Junwei Zheng,Weijia Fan,Kunyu Peng,Di Wen,Jiale Wei,Jiaming Zhang,Rainer Stiefelhagen*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: SGR3 is a training-free, RAG-enhanced MLLM pipeline that generates 3D scene graphs without explicit 3D reconstruction by retrieving semantically similar scene graphs and reasoning over them; a weighted patch-level similarity scheme improves retrieval robustness, yielding performance competitive with training-free baselines and comparable to GNN-based expert models.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 3D scene graphs are valuable for robot reasoning but current methods depend on multi-modal inputs, explicit 3D reconstruction, and heuristic graph construction that constrain relation prediction and limit applicability when data are scarce or noisy. A lighter-weight, training-free approach with stronger semantic reasoning is sought.

Method: Use an MLLM with retrieval-augmented generation: a ColPali-style cross-modal retriever fetches semantically aligned scene graphs from a knowledge base given scene inputs; a weighted patch-level similarity selection downweights blurry/uninformative regions; the MLLM conditions on retrieved graphs to produce semantic relationship triplets, bypassing explicit 3D reconstruction.

Result: Competitive with training-free baselines and on par with GNN expert models; ablations over the retriever and knowledge base scale show that external retrieved information is explicitly used during token generation rather than being implicitly absorbed.

Conclusion: A reconstruction-free, training-free RAG+MLLM pipeline can produce high-quality 3D scene graphs and reduce dependence on heuristics and multi-modal data; retrieval quality and KB size are key, and explicit integration of retrieved content drives reasoning performance.

Abstract: 3D scene graphs provide a structured representation of object entities and their relationships, enabling high-level interpretation and reasoning for robots while remaining intuitively understandable to humans. Existing approaches for 3D scene graph generation typically combine scene reconstruction with graph neural networks (GNNs). However, such pipelines require multi-modal data that may not always be available, and their reliance on heuristic graph construction can constrain the prediction of relationship triplets. In this work, we introduce a Scene Graph Retrieval-Reasoning Model in 3D (SGR3 Model), a training-free framework that leverages multi-modal large language models (MLLMs) with retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) for semantic scene graph generation. SGR3 Model bypasses the need for explicit 3D reconstruction. Instead, it enhances relational reasoning by incorporating semantically aligned scene graphs retrieved via a ColPali-style cross-modal framework. To improve retrieval robustness, we further introduce a weighted patch-level similarity selection mechanism that mitigates the negative impact of blurry or semantically uninformative regions. Experiments demonstrate that SGR3 Model achieves competitive performance compared to training-free baselines and on par with GNN-based expert models. Moreover, an ablation study on the retrieval module and knowledge base scale reveals that retrieved external information is explicitly integrated into the token generation process, rather than being implicitly internalized through abstraction.

</details>


### [9] [Spinverse: Differentiable Physics for Permeability-Aware Microstructure Reconstruction from Diffusion MRI](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04638)
*Prathamesh Pradeep Khole,Mario M. Brenes,Zahra Kais Petiwala,Ehsan Mirafzali,Utkarsh Gupta,Jing-Rebecca Li,Andrada Ianus,Razvan Marinescu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Spinverse learns permeable microstructural interfaces from dMRI by backpropagating through a differentiable Bloch–Torrey PDE on a fixed tetrahedral mesh, using face-wise permeabilities and priors/curriculum to stabilize inversion; on synthetic data it reconstructs accurate boundaries and valid structures.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing dMRI approaches often assume impermeable barriers or recover only voxel-averaged parameters, failing to explicitly delineate microstructural interfaces or handle permeability. The goal is to recover geometries (and their permeability) directly from signals without predefining boundary topology.

Method: Represent tissue on a fixed tetrahedral grid; assign each interior face a learnable permeability. Use a fully differentiable Bloch–Torrey simulator to forward-model signals and optimize a signal-matching loss via backpropagation. Extract interfaces by thresholding the learned permeability field. Add mesh-based geometric priors to regularize this ill-posed problem and apply a staged multi-sequence optimization curriculum to avoid local minima.

Result: Across synthetic voxel meshes, Spinverse reconstructs diverse geometries; proper sequence scheduling and regularization prevent outline-only solutions and improve boundary accuracy and structural plausibility.

Conclusion: Permeability-aware, PDE-based inversion can recover explicit microstructural interfaces from dMRI without altering mesh connectivity. Regularization and curriculum are crucial. Results on synthetic data indicate promise for more realistic, permeability-sensitive microstructure reconstructions.

Abstract: Diffusion MRI (dMRI) is sensitive to microstructural barriers, yet most existing methods either assume impermeable boundaries or estimate voxel-level parameters without recovering explicit interfaces. We present Spinverse, a permeability-aware reconstruction method that inverts dMRI measurements through a fully differentiable Bloch-Torrey simulator. Spinverse represents tissue on a fixed tetrahedral grid and treats each interior face permeability as a learnable parameter; low-permeability faces act as diffusion barriers, so microstructural boundaries whose topology is not fixed a priori (up to the resolution of the ambient mesh) emerge without changing mesh connectivity or vertex positions. Given a target signal, we optimize face permeabilities by backpropagating a signal-matching loss through the PDE forward model, and recover an interface by thresholding the learned permeability field. To mitigate the ill-posedness of permeability inversion, we use mesh-based geometric priors; to avoid local minima, we use a staged multi-sequence optimization curriculum. Across a collection of synthetic voxel meshes, Spinverse reconstructs diverse geometries and demonstrates that sequence scheduling and regularization are critical to avoid outline-only solutions while improving both boundary accuracy and structural validity.

</details>


### [10] [sFRC for assessing hallucinations in medical image restoration](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04673)
*Prabhat Kc,Rongping Zeng,Nirmal Soni,Aldo Badano*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Introduces sFRC, a patchwise Fourier Ring Correlation–based scanning method to localize and quantify hallucinations in deep-learning medical image reconstructions; validated on CT and MR tasks and shown to generalize beyond DL to conventional and unrolled methods.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: DL reconstructions can look plausibly clean yet contain hallucinated structures, and the field lacks easy, robust, and quantitative tools to detect such artifacts, especially under sparse/undersampled acquisitions and OOD data.

Method: Compute Fourier Ring Correlation on small image patches while scanning across a DL reconstruction and a corresponding reference to generate local agreement maps; set detection parameters via expert-annotated hallucinations or imaging-theory–derived maps; apply to CT super-resolution, CT sparse-view, and MRI subsampled restoration to flag regions where high-frequency content is unsupported by data; summarize with hallucination rates.

Result: sFRC detects hallucinated features in CT tasks, aligns with theory-based hallucination maps in MRI, quantifies higher hallucination rates in OOD settings and with stronger undersampling, and remains effective for a classical regularized method and a state-of-the-art unrolled approach.

Conclusion: sFRC provides a practical, modality- and method-agnostic framework to localize and quantify hallucinations, enabling robustness assessment of reconstruction pipelines and offering a data-consistency check complementary to subjective image quality.

Abstract: Deep learning (DL) methods are currently being explored to restore images from sparse-view-, limited-data-, and undersampled-based acquisitions in medical applications. Although outputs from DL may appear visually appealing based on likability/subjective criteria (such as less noise, smooth features), they may also suffer from hallucinations. This issue is further exacerbated by a lack of easy-to-use techniques and robust metrics for the identification of hallucinations in DL outputs. In this work, we propose performing Fourier Ring Correlation (FRC) analysis over small patches and concomitantly (s)canning across DL outputs and their reference counterparts to detect hallucinations (termed as sFRC). We describe the rationale behind sFRC and provide its mathematical formulation. The parameters essential to sFRC may be set using predefined hallucinated features annotated by subject matter experts or using imaging theory-based hallucination maps. We use sFRC to detect hallucinations for three undersampled medical imaging problems: CT super-resolution, CT sparse view, and MRI subsampled restoration. In the testing phase, we demonstrate sFRC's effectiveness in detecting hallucinated features for the CT problem and sFRC's agreement with imaging theory-based outputs on hallucinated feature maps for the MR problem. Finally, we quantify the hallucination rates of DL methods on in-distribution versus out-of-distribution data and under increasing subsampling rates to characterize the robustness of DL methods. Beyond DL-based methods, sFRC's effectiveness in detecting hallucinations for a conventional regularization-based restoration method and a state-of-the-art unrolled method is also shown.

</details>


### [11] [Decoding the Pulse of Reasoning VLMs in Multi-Image Understanding Tasks](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04676)
*Chenjun Li*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: PulseFocus is a training-free, inference-time method that structures chain-of-thought for multi-image VLMs into plan/focus blocks and softly gates text-to-image attention to the referenced image, reducing diffuse “pulses” and positional bias and improving accuracy on multi-image benchmarks (BLINK +3.7%, MuirBench +1.07%).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Multi-image reasoning in VLMs is hindered by unfocused, sporadic T2I attention during CoT and a systematic positional bias across images, which likely undermines grounded reasoning. A lightweight way to steer attention without retraining is needed.

Method: Introduce interleaved plan/focus blocks during decoding: (1) plan step explicitly names which image to inspect; (2) focus step applies soft gating that amplifies attention to the referenced image while attenuating others during token generation. This is applied at inference only, requiring no additional training.

Result: Sharper, more concentrated attention during CoT and consistent accuracy gains on multi-image benchmarks: BLINK benchmark improves by +3.7% and MuirBench by +1.07%.

Conclusion: Managing and gating attention during CoT materially improves multi-image reasoning. Explicit planning plus soft attention gating is a simple, training-free control that mitigates diffuse pulses and positional bias, suggesting broader opportunities for controllable attention in VLM reasoning.

Abstract: Multi-image reasoning remains a significant challenge for vision-language models (VLMs). We investigate a previously overlooked phenomenon: during chain-of-thought (CoT) generation, the text-to-image (T2I) attention of reasoning VLMs exhibits diffuse "pulses": sporadic and unfocused attention patterns that fail to concentrate on task-relevant images. We further reveal a systematic positional bias in attention allocation across images. Motivated by these observations, we propose PulseFocus, a training-free, inference-time method that structures CoT reasoning into interleaved plan/focus blocks with soft attention gating. By forcing the model to explicitly plan which image to examine and then gating decode-time attention to the referenced image, PulseFocus sharpens attention focus and yields consistent improvements on multi-image benchmarks like BLINK benchmark (+3.7%) and MuirBench (+1.07%).

</details>


### [12] [A Benchmark Study of Neural Network Compression Methods for Hyperspectral Image Classification](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04720)
*Sai Shi*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Evaluates pruning, quantization, and knowledge distillation on CNNs for hyperspectral land cover classification, showing substantial size/compute reductions with competitive accuracy on two benchmarks and mapping trade-offs between compression and performance.


<details>

Result: Compressed models markedly reduce model size and computational cost while maintaining competitive classification accuracy; the study quantifies trade-offs among compression ratio, efficiency, and accuracy.

Abstract: Deep neural networks have achieved strong performance in image classification tasks due to their ability to learn complex patterns from high-dimensional data. However, their large computational and memory requirements often limit deployment on resource-constrained platforms such as remote sensing devices and edge systems. Network compression techniques have therefore been proposed to reduce model size and computational cost while maintaining predictive performance. In this study, we conduct a systematic evaluation of neural network compression methods for a remote sensing application, namely hyperspectral land cover classification. Our results demonstrate that compressed models can significantly reduce model size and computational cost while maintaining competitive classification performance. These findings provide insights into the trade-offs between compression ratio, efficiency, and accuracy, and highlight the potential of compression techniques for enabling efficient deep learning deployment in remote sensing applications.

We investigate how prompt specificity and temporal window lengths (1s--3s) influence performance, focusing on the precision--recall trade-off. Our findings reveal a pronounced conservative bias in zero-shot settings; while models exhibit high confidence, they disproportionately favor the 'normal' class, resulting in high precision but a recall collapse that limits practical utility. ### [14] [FOZO: Forward-Only Zeroth-Order Prompt Optimization for Test-Time Adaptation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04733)
*Xingyu Wang,Tao Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: FOZO is a forward-only, backprop-free test-time adaptation method that optimizes prompts via zeroth-order estimation with a decaying perturbation scale, aligning feature statistics and reducing prediction entropy. It achieves state-of-the-art accuracy under distribution shift while being memory- and compute-efficient, including on INT8 models.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Test-time adaptation is needed to handle distribution shifts in real-world deployment, but existing methods either rely on costly backpropagation that changes model weights—unsuitable for low-resource devices—or are backprop-free yet weak at adaptation. The paper seeks a practical, strong, and resource-friendly TTA approach.

Method: Introduce Forward-Only Zeroth-Order Optimization (FOZO): a backpropagation-free, prompt-based TTA that estimates gradients via zeroth-order finite-difference perturbations. The optimization is guided by objectives on intermediate feature statistics and prediction entropy. A dynamically decaying perturbation scale stabilizes and accelerates adaptation, with convergence proved under a TTA data-stream assumption.

Result: On continual adaptation benchmarks ImageNet-C, ImageNet-R, and ImageNet-Sketch, FOZO outperforms prominent gradient-based TTA and the state-of-the-art forward-only FOA. It reaches 59.52% Top-1 on ImageNet-C (5K, level 5), surpassing FOA (58.13%), and shows strong performance on quantized INT8 models.

However, current approaches face significant limitations: backpropagation-based methods are not suitable for low-end deployment devices, due to their high computation and memory requirements, as well as their tendency to modify model weights during adaptation; while traditional backpropagation-free techniques exhibit constrained adaptation capabilities. In this work, we propose Forward-Only Zeroth-Order Optimization (FOZO), a novel and practical backpropagation-free paradigm for TTA. FOZO leverages a memory-efficient zeroth-order prompt optimization, which is led by objectives optimizing both intermediate feature statistics and prediction entropy. To ensure efficient and stable adaptation over the out-of-distribution data stream, we introduce a dynamically decaying perturbation scale during zeroth-order gradient estimation and theoretically prove its convergence under the TTA data stream assumption. Extensive continual adaptation experiments on ImageNet-C, ImageNet-R, and ImageNet-Sketch demonstrate FOZO's superior performance, achieving 59.52% Top-1 accuracy on ImageNet-C (5K, level 5) and outperforming main gradient-based methods and SOTA forward-only FOA (58.13%). Furthermore, FOZO exhibits strong generalization on quantized (INT8) models. These findings demonstrate that FOZO is a highly competitive solution for TTA deployment in resource-limited scenarios.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Prior IISR works train on simulated data or treat IR like visible imagery, overlooking IR-specific physics and real degradations, leading to domain gaps and physically inconsistent reconstructions. There is a need for methods and datasets that handle real, non-uniform degradations while preserving thermal consistency.

Key components: (1) Thermal-Structural Guidance module that encodes thermal priors to alleviate mismatch between thermal radiation and intensity edges; (2) Condition-Adaptive Codebook that dynamically modulates discrete representations using degradation-aware thermal priors to mitigate quantization bias from non-uniform degradations; (3) Thermal Order Consistency Loss that enforces a monotonic relationship between temperature and pixel intensity, preserving relative brightness order under spatial misalignment and thermal drift. Abstract: Infrared image super-resolution (IISR) under real-world conditions is a practically significant yet rarely addressed task. Pioneering works are often trained and evaluated on simulated datasets or neglect the intrinsic differences between infrared and visible imaging. In practice, however, real infrared images are affected by coupled optical and sensing degradations that jointly deteriorate both structural sharpness and thermal fidelity. To address these challenges, we propose Real-IISR, a unified autoregressive framework for real-world IISR that progressively reconstructs fine-grained thermal structures and clear backgrounds in a scale-by-scale manner via thermal-structural guided visual autoregression. Specifically, a Thermal-Structural Guidance module encodes thermal priors to mitigate the mismatch between thermal radiation and structural edges. Since non-uniform degradations typically induce quantization bias, Real-IISR adopts a Condition-Adaptive Codebook that dynamically modulates discrete representations based on degradation-aware thermal priors. Also, a Thermal Order Consistency Loss enforces a monotonic relation between temperature and pixel intensity, ensuring relative brightness order rather than absolute values to maintain physical consistency under spatial misalignment and thermal drift. We build FLIR-IISR, a real-world IISR dataset with paired LR-HR infrared images acquired via automated focus variation and motion-induced blur. Extensive experiments demonstrate the promising performance of Real-IISR, providing a unified foundation for real-world IISR and benchmarking. The dataset and code are available at: https://github.com/JZD151/Real-IISR.

These findings indicate that while GPT-5 represents a meaningful advance toward integrated multimodal clinical reasoning, mirroring the clinician's cognitive process of biasing uncertain information with objective findings, generalist models are not yet substitutes for purpose-built systems in highly specialized, perception-critical tasks.

Specifically, the method identifies Onset and Apex frames, which are characterized by significant micro-expression variation, from complete micro-expression action sequences via a dynamic frame reselection mechanism. It then uses these to determine Offset frames and construct a rich spatio-temporal dynamic representation. A two-branch structure with shared parameters is then used to efficiently extract spatio-temporal features. Extensive experiments are conducted on seven widely recognized micro-expression datasets. Furthermore, quantitative analyses confirm that offset-frame annotations in multicultural datasets are more uncertain, providing theoretical justification for standardizing micro-expression annotations. These findings directly support our argument for reconsidering the validity and generalizability of dataset annotation paradigms. Notably, this design can be integrated into existing models without increasing the number of parameters, offering a new approach to enhancing micro-expression recognition performance. The source code is available on GitHub[https://github.com/Cross-Innovation-Lab/GAMDSS].

Extensive experiments on two clinical DSA datasets demonstrate that DSA-SRGS significantly outperforms state-of-the-art methods in both quantitative metrics and qualitative visual fidelity.

### [22] [LAW & ORDER: Adaptive Spatial Weighting for Medical Diffusion and Segmentation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04795)
*Anugunj Naman,Ayushman Singh,Gaibo Zhang,Yaguang Zhang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Addresses lesion–background imbalance in medical imaging by learning where to focus training and inference, improving both diffusion-based synthesis and segmentation with lightweight adapters.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Segmentation and controllable image synthesis in medical imaging suffer from severe spatial imbalance: small lesions amid large backgrounds. Diffusion models deviate from intended lesion layouts, and segmenters underperform in spatially uncertain regions. The authors aim to adaptively allocate attention/loss to the most informative pixels to counteract this imbalance.

Method: Propose two plug-in adapters: (1) Learnable Adaptive Weighter (LAW) for diffusion training that predicts per-pixel loss weights from features and lesion masks; it uses normalization, clamping, and regularization to avoid degenerate weighting. (2) Optimal Region Detection with Efficient Resolution (ORDER) for segmentation that applies selective bidirectional skip attention at late decoder stages to focus on uncertain/critical regions while keeping computation low.

Result: On polyp and kidney tumor datasets: LAW improves FID by ~20% vs. uniform weighting (52.28 vs. 65.60) and synthetic images boost downstream segmentation Dice by 4.9% (83.2% vs. 78.3%). ORDER yields a 6.0% Dice gain on MK-UNet (81.3% vs. 75.3%) with only 0.56 GFLOPs and 42K params, remaining ~730× smaller than nnUNet.

Abstract: Medical image analysis relies on accurate segmentation, and benefits from controllable synthesis (of new training images). Yet both tasks of the cyclical pipeline face spatial imbalance: lesions occupy small regions against vast backgrounds. In particular, diffusion models have been shown to drift from prescribed lesion layouts, while efficient segmenters struggle on spatially uncertain regions. Adaptive spatial weighting addresses this by learning where to allocate computational resources. This paper introduces a pair of network adapters: 1) Learnable Adaptive Weighter (LAW) which predicts per-pixel loss modulation from features and masks for diffusion training, stabilized via a mix of normalization, clamping, and regularization to prevent degenerate solutions; and 2) Optimal Region Detection with Efficient Resolution (ORDER) which applies selective bidirectional skip attention at late decoder stages for efficient segmentation. Experiments on polyp and kidney tumor datasets demonstrate that LAW achieves 20% FID generative improvement over a uniform baseline (52.28 vs. 65.60), with synthetic data then improving downstream segmentation by 4.9% Dice coefficient (83.2% vs. 78.3%). ORDER reaches 6.0% Dice improvement on MK-UNet (81.3% vs. 75.3%) with 0.56 GFLOPs and just 42K parameters, remaining 730x smaller than the standard nnUNet.

</details>

### [24] [MASQuant: Modality-Aware Smoothing Quantization for Multimodal Large Language Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04800)
*Lulu Hu,Wenhu Xiao,Xin Chen,Xinhua Xu,Bowen Xu,Kun Li,Yongliang Tao*

Main category: cs.CV

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: PTQ methods that work for text‑only LLMs degrade on MLLMs because different modalities have distinct activation statistics. Using a single smoothing factor (as in SmoothQuant) misaligns modalities and breaks computational invariance across them. A modality‑sensitive quantization strategy is needed to preserve accuracy without fine‑tuning.

Method: Propose Modality‑Aware Smoothing Quantization (MASQuant) with two components: (1) Modality‑Aware Smoothing (MAS) that learns separate, modality‑specific smoothing factors (using calibration) to avoid smoothing misalignment; (2) Cross‑Modal Compensation (CMC) that applies SVD whitening to convert inter‑modal activation differences into low‑rank forms, enabling unified quantization across modalities while maintaining computational invariance. Works as a PTQ pipeline for dual‑ and tri‑modal MLLMs.

Result: MASQuant delivers stable quantization quality across multi‑modal settings and is competitive with state‑of‑the‑art PTQ approaches on MLLMs, per reported experiments.

Conclusion: Addressing modality heterogeneity via modality‑aware smoothing plus SVD‑based cross‑modal compensation makes PTQ viable for MLLMs, providing consistent performance across modalities with open‑sourced code.

Abstract: Post-training quantization (PTQ) with computational invariance for Large Language Models~(LLMs) have demonstrated remarkable advances, however, their application to Multimodal Large Language Models~(MLLMs) presents substantial challenges. In this paper, we analyze SmoothQuant as a case study and identify two critical issues: Smoothing Misalignment and Cross-Modal Computational Invariance. To address these issues, we propose Modality-Aware Smoothing Quantization (MASQuant), a novel framework that introduces (1) Modality-Aware Smoothing (MAS), which learns separate, modality-specific smoothing factors to prevent Smoothing Misalignment, and (2) Cross-Modal Compensation (CMC), which addresses Cross-modal Computational Invariance by using SVD whitening to transform multi-modal activation differences into low-rank forms, enabling unified quantization across modalities. MASQuant demonstrates stable quantization performance across both dual-modal and tri-modal MLLMs. Experimental results show that MASQuant is competitive among the state-of-the-art PTQ algorithms. Source code: https://github.com/alibaba/EfficientAI.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: CLIP’s visual encoder underperforms due to limited capacity in both discriminating classes and perceiving fine details. Prior diffusion-enhanced representation methods condition reconstruction on CLIP tokens but can erode discriminative power. The paper seeks a way to enhance both discriminative and perceptual abilities without trading one for the other.

Method: Start with diffusion-based image reconstruction augmented by contrastive learning, observe gradient conflict. Propose DCR: a unified objective where contrastive signals are computed from each reconstructed image (not the original) and injected into the diffusion process. Provide theoretical analysis showing DCR jointly optimizes discriminative and perceptual abilities.

This capacity includes both Discriminative Ability (D-Ability), which reflects class separability, and Detail Perceptual Ability (P-Ability), which focuses on fine-grained visual cues. Recent solutions use diffusion models to enhance representations by conditioning image reconstruction on CLIP visual tokens. We argue that such paradigms may compromise D-Ability and therefore fail to effectively address CLIP's representation limitations. To address this, we integrate contrastive signals into diffusion-based reconstruction to pursue more comprehensive visual representations. We begin with a straightforward design that augments the diffusion process with contrastive learning on input images. However, empirical results show that the naive combination suffers from gradient conflict and yields suboptimal performance. To balance the optimization, we introduce the Diffusion Contrastive Reconstruction (DCR), which unifies the learning objective. The key idea is to inject contrastive signals derived from each reconstructed image, rather than from the original input, into the diffusion process. Our theoretical analysis shows that the DCR loss can jointly optimize D-Ability and P-Ability. Extensive experiments across various benchmarks and multi-modal large language models validate the effectiveness of our method. The code is available at https://github.com/boyuh/DCR.

This situation raises questions about the necessity of polarization cues, which require specialized hardware and have limited training data. First, existing synthetic datasets use limited and unrealistic 3D objects, with simple geometry and random texture maps that do not match the underlying shapes. Second, real-world polarization signals are often affected by sensor noise, which is not well modeled during training. To address the first issue, we render a high-quality polarization dataset using 1,954 3D-scanned real-world objects. We further incorporate pretrained DINOv3 priors to improve generalization to unseen objects. To address the second issue, we introduce polarization sensor-aware data augmentation that better reflects real-world conditions. Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: CAD is a framework for instance-dependent partial label learning that disentangles overlapping class evidence by class-specific augmentations (intra-class alignment) and a weighted penalty on ambiguous labels (inter-class separation), yielding clearer class boundaries and better accuracy.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: In ID-PLL, candidate labels are correlated with instance features. Similar classes often share features and candidate sets, causing instance entanglement and class confusion. Existing methods insufficiently enforce within-class consistency and between-class separation under ambiguity.

Method: Class-specific Augmentation based Disentanglement (CAD): (1) Intra-class regulation—amplify class-specific features to create class-wise augmentations and align augmentations across instances of the same class; (2) Inter-class regulation—use a weighted penalty loss assigning stronger penalties to more ambiguous labels to enlarge inter-class distances. Both are jointly optimized to disentangle representations.

Result: Extensive experiments show CAD effectively mitigates entanglement and improves ID-PLL performance across benchmarks. (Abstract reports qualitative and aggregate gains; specific metrics not provided.)

Conclusion: By combining intra-class alignment with inter-class penalization, CAD sharpens class boundaries, reduces confusion from entanglement, and advances state-of-the-art performance for ID-PLL. Code is publicly available.

Abstract: Partial label learning is a prominent weakly supervised classification task, where each training instance is ambiguously labeled with a set of candidate labels. In real-world scenarios, candidate labels are often influenced by instance features, leading to the emergence of instance-dependent PLL (ID-PLL), a setting that more accurately reflects this relationship. A significant challenge in ID-PLL is instance entanglement, where instances from similar classes share overlapping features and candidate labels, resulting in increased class confusion. To address this issue, we propose a novel Class-specific Augmentation based Disentanglement (CAD) framework, which tackles instance entanglement by both intra- and inter-class regulations. For intra-class regulation, CAD amplifies class-specific features to generate class-wise augmentations and aligns same-class augmentations across instances. For inter-class regulation, CAD introduces a weighted penalty loss function that applies stronger penalties to more ambiguous labels, encouraging larger inter-class distances. By jointly applying intra- and inter-class regulations, CAD improves the clarity of class boundaries and reduces class confusion caused by entanglement. Extensive experimental results demonstrate the effectiveness of CAD in mitigating the entanglement problem and enhancing ID-PLL performance. The code is available at https://github.com/RyanZhaoIc/CAD.git.

To address this issue, we propose a Semantic-Augmented Dynamic Contrastive Attack (SADCA) that enhances adversarial transferability through progressive and semantically guided perturbation. SADCA progressively disrupts cross-modal alignment through dynamic interactions between adversarial images and texts. This straightforward setting naturally restricts the richness of feature representations, delivering limits on the search space and thus impeding the diversity of adversarial perturbations. Conclusion: By replacing metadata with learned prompt features, PNG improves generalizability and practicality of noise synthesis and benefits downstream denoising across varied real-world scenarios.

Abstract: Denoising in the sRGB image space is challenging due to noise variability. Although end-to-end methods perform well, their effectiveness in real-world scenarios is limited by the scarcity of real noisy-clean image pairs, which are expensive and difficult to collect. To address this limitation, several generative methods have been developed to synthesize realistic noisy images from limited data. These generative approaches often rely on camera metadata during both training and testing to synthesize real-world noise. However, the lack of metadata or inconsistencies between devices restricts their usability. Therefore, we propose a novel framework called Prompt-Driven Noise Generation (PNG). This model is capable of acquiring high-dimensional prompt features that capture the characteristics of real-world input noise and creating a variety of realistic noisy images consistent with the distribution of the input noise. By eliminating the dependency on explicit camera metadata, our approach significantly enhances the generalizability and applicability of noise synthesis. Comprehensive experiments reveal that our model effectively produces realistic noisy images and show the successful application of these generated images in removing real-world noise across various benchmark datasets.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Pipeline: (1) recover monocular 3D pose sequences using a diffusion-based backbone; (2) automatically detect pitching events; (3) extract and validate 229 biomechanical features; (4) classify eight pitch types with gradient-boosted trees; (5) perform feature-importance analysis partitioned by body region and biomechanical attribute; (6) test separability of grip-defined variants (four-seam vs two-seam).

A systematic importance analysis reveals that upper-body mechanics contribute 64.9\% of the predictive signal versus 35.1\% for the lower body, with wrist position (14.8\%) and trunk lateral tilt emerging as the most informative joint group and biomechanical feature, respectively. This work introduces a novel two-stage (structure- and report-learning) framework tailored for CTRG featuring effective structure-wise image-text contrasting. In the first stage, a set of learnable structure-specific visual queries observe corresponding structures in a CT image. The resulting observation tokens are contrasted with structure-specific textual features extracted from the accompanying radiology report with a structure-wise image-text contrastive loss. In addition, text-text similarity-based soft pseudo targets are proposed to mitigate the impact of false negatives, i.e., semantically identical image structures and texts from non-paired images and reports. Thus, the model learns structure-level semantic correspondences between CT images and reports. Further, a dynamic, diversity-enhanced negative queue is proposed to guide the network in learning to discriminate various abnormalities. In the second stage, the visual structure queries are frozen and used to select the critical image patch embeddings depicting each anatomical structure, minimizing distractions from irrelevant areas while reducing memory consumption. Also, a text decoder is added and trained for report generation.Our extensive experiments on two public datasets demonstrate that our framework establishes new state-of-the-art performance for CTRG in clinical efficiency, and its components are effective.

### [38] [Federated Modality-specific Encoders and Partially Personalized Fusion Decoder for Multimodal Brain Tumor Segmentation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04887)
*Hong Liu,Dong Wei,Qian Dai,Xian Wu,Yefeng Zheng,Liansheng Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: FedMEPD is a federated learning framework for multimodal medical imaging that uses modality-specific encoders (fully federated) and partially personalized fusion decoders, plus server-distributed multimodal “anchors” to help clients with missing modalities via cross-attention; it outperforms recent baselines on BraTS 2018/2020 brain tumor segmentation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Real-world FL participants often lack some imaging modalities, creating intermodal heterogeneity that current FL methods (focused mostly on intramodal/client data heterogeneity) do not address. Simultaneously, each site desires a personalized model tailored to its local data. The work aims to jointly handle missing modalities and personalization in FL for multimodal imaging.

Method: - Assign a dedicated encoder per modality; encoders are globally federated across clients to learn modality-invariant representations.
- Use decoders that are partially personalized: a discrepancy measure between global and local updates selects which decoder filters remain local vs. global.
- A central server with full-modal data employs a fusion decoder to backpropagate through all encoders, aligning modalities.
- The server extracts multiple “anchors” from fused multimodal features and shares them with clients.
- Clients with incomplete modalities calibrate missing-modal features toward these global anchors using scaled dot-product cross-attention, compensating for absent modalities.

Result: On BraTS 2018 and 2020 brain tumor segmentation, the proposed framework surpasses various recent methods for both multimodal and personalized FL; ablations suggest each component (modality-specific encoders, partial personalization, and anchor-based calibration) contributes to the gains.

Conclusion: FedMEPD effectively addresses both intermodal heterogeneity and client personalization in federated multimodal medical image analysis. By federating modality-specific encoders, selectively personalizing decoders, and aligning missing-modal information via anchor-guided cross-attention, it improves segmentation performance over strong baselines.

Abstract: Most existing federated learning (FL) methods for medical image analysis only considered intramodal heterogeneity, limiting their applicability to multimodal imaging applications. In practice, some FL participants may possess only a subset of the complete imaging modalities, posing intermodal heterogeneity as a challenge to effectively training a global model on all participants' data. Meanwhile, each participant expects a personalized model tailored to its local data characteristics in FL. This work proposes a new FL framework with federated modality-specific encoders and partially personalized multimodal fusion decoders (FedMEPD) to address the two concurrent issues. Specifically, FedMEPD employs an exclusive encoder for each modality to account for the intermodal heterogeneity. While these encoders are fully federated, the decoders are partially personalized to meet individual needs -- using the discrepancy between global and local parameter updates to dynamically determine which decoder filters are personalized. Implementation-wise, a server with full-modal data employs a fusion decoder to fuse representations from all modality-specific encoders, thus bridging the modalities to optimize the encoders via backpropagation. Moreover, multiple anchors are extracted from the fused multimodal representations and distributed to the clients in addition to the model parameters. Conversely, the clients with incomplete modalities calibrate their missing-modal representations toward the global full-modal anchors via scaled dot-product cross-attention, making up for the information loss due to absent modalities. FedMEPD is validated on the BraTS 2018 and 2020 multimodal brain tumor segmentation benchmarks. Results show that it outperforms various up-to-date methods for multimodal and personalized FL, and its novel designs are effective.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Global self‑attention in ViTs excels at long‑range dependencies but can blur fine local details that segmentation needs. The goal is to retrofit classification‑trained ViTs for stronger dense prediction without altering the standard training regime or sacrificing image‑level accuracy.

Method: Introduce a plug‑in that (1) modulates self‑attention with a learnable Gaussian kernel centered on each query to bias attention toward nearby patches, and (2) refines patch representations to learn better spatial/positional embeddings. This preserves global context while strengthening local focus; applied after standard image‑level training.

Abstract: Vision transformers have demonstrated remarkable success in classification by leveraging global self-attention to capture long-range dependencies. However, this same mechanism can obscure fine-grained spatial details crucial for tasks such as segmentation. In this work, we seek to enhance segmentation performance of vision transformers after standard image-level classification training. More specifically, we present a simple yet effective add-on that improves performance on segmentation tasks while retaining vision transformers' image-level recognition capabilities. In our approach, we modulate the self-attention with a learnable Gaussian kernel that biases the attention toward neighboring patches. We further refine the patch representations to learn better embeddings at patch positions. These modifications encourage tokens to focus on local surroundings and ensure meaningful representations at spatial positions, while still preserving the model's ability to incorporate global information. Experiments demonstrate the effectiveness of our modifications, evidenced by substantial segmentation gains on three benchmarks (e.g., over 6% and 4% on ADE20K for ViT Tiny and Base), without changing the training regime or sacrificing classification performance. The code is available at https://github.com/sinahmr/LocAtViT/.

  <summary>Details</summary>

The authors observe that tokens corresponding to real objects naturally pay more attention to the generated text than hallucinated ones, suggesting generated text carries instruction-relevant visual and contextual cues worth leveraging.

Method: 1) Analyze attention maps to show real-object tokens attend more to generated text than hallucinated tokens. 2) Propose IAT (Attention to Generated Text) that amplifies attention to generated text tokens during inference to reduce hallucinations while maintaining coherence. 3) Introduce AdaIAT, which sets layer-wise intervention thresholds and per-head amplification magnitudes, enabling fine-grained, timing-aware control that avoids degrading innate prediction abilities.

Result: Across multiple LVLMs, the approach lowers hallucination without inducing repetition or hurting language quality. On LLaVA-1.5, hallucination metrics C_S and C_I drop by 35.8% and 37.1%, respectively, while linguistic performance and prediction capability are preserved.

Abstract: Hallucination has been a significant impediment to the development and application of current Large Vision-Language Models (LVLMs). To mitigate hallucinations, one intuitive and effective way is to directly increase attention weights to image tokens during inference. Although this effectively reduces the hallucination rate, it often induces repetitive descriptions. To address this, we first conduct an analysis of attention patterns and reveal that real object tokens tend to assign higher attention to the generated text than hallucinated ones. This inspires us to leverage the generated text, which contains instruction-related visual information and contextual knowledge, to alleviate hallucinations while maintaining linguistic coherence. We therefore propose Attention to Generated Text (IAT) and demonstrate that it significantly reduces the hallucination rate while avoiding repetitive descriptions. To prevent naive amplification from impairing the inherent prediction capabilities of LVLMs, we further explore Adaptive IAT (AdaIAT) that employs a layer-wise threshold to control intervention time and fine-grained amplification magnitude tailored to the characteristics of each attention head. Both analysis and experiments demonstrate the effectiveness of AdaIAT. Results of several LVLMs show that AdaIAT effectively alleviates hallucination (reducing hallucination rates $C_S$ and $C_I$ on LLaVA-1.5 by 35.8% and 37.1%, respectively) while preserving linguistic performance and prediction capability, achieving an attractive trade-off.

TL;DR: Adds a “shrinkage” parameter to orthographic projection to mimic perspective in monocular 3DMM regression, enabling stable and accurate fitting on close-up/head‑mounted camera footage; validated with quantitative and qualitative results on a custom dataset and supported by finetuning strategies.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Orthographic projection is robust for 3DMM regression because it avoids focal-length–distance ambiguity, but it fails on close-up facial views (e.g., head‑mounted cameras) where perspective distortion is strong. There’s a need to capture perspective effects without sacrificing the stability of orthographic models.

Method: Extend standard orthographic projection with a learnable shrinkage parameter that induces a pseudo‑perspective effect while retaining the numerical stability of orthographic projection. Provide techniques to finetune existing monocular 3DMM regression models under this new camera model.

Result: Compared to baseline orthographic approaches, the proposed model achieves better alignment and reconstruction on close-up facial imagery, as shown by both quantitative metrics and qualitative examples on a custom head‑mounted camera dataset.

Conclusion: A lightweight camera-model modification (orthographic + shrinkage) effectively captures perspective in close-up settings, making monocular 3DMM regression more accurate and stable for head‑mounted footage without the pitfalls of full perspective modeling.

Abstract: We introduce a novel camera model for monocular 3D Morphable Model (3DMM) regression methods that effectively captures the perspective distortion effect commonly seen in close-up facial images.
  Fitting 3D morphable models to video is a key technique in content creation. In particular, regression-based approaches have produced fast and accurate results by matching the rendered output of the morphable model to the target image. These methods typically achieve stable performance with orthographic projection, which eliminates the ambiguity between focal length and object distance. However, this simplification makes them unsuitable for close-up footage, such as that captured with head-mounted cameras.
  We extend orthographic projection with a new shrinkage parameter, incorporating a pseudo-perspective effect while preserving the stability of the original projection. We present several techniques that allow finetuning of existing models, and demonstrate the effectiveness of our modification through both quantitative and qualitative comparisons using a custom dataset recorded with head-mounted cameras.

### [47] [BiEvLight: Bi-level Learning of Task-Aware Event Refinement for Low-Light Image Enhancement](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04975)
*Zishu Yao,Xiang-Xiang Su,Shengning Zhou,Guang-Yong Chen,Guodong Fan,Xing Chen*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: BiEvLight jointly enhances low-light images and denoises event streams via a task-aware, bilevel optimization that uses image–event gradient correlation to suppress event BA noise and reduce noise coupling during fusion, achieving SOTA gains on a real-world dataset.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Event cameras promise robust guidance for low-light image enhancement thanks to high dynamic range, but real event streams contain background activity (BA) noise, and low-light images have low SNR. When fused, these noises couple and limit performance. Static, pre-processing event denoising cannot adapt to the enhancement goal and faces over/under-denoising trade-offs. Hence, accurate, task-adaptive event denoising is needed to unlock event-based fusion benefits.

Method: Propose BiEvLight: a hierarchical, task-aware framework that couples event denoising with image enhancement. 1) Leverage the strong gradient correlation between images and events to construct a gradient-guided event denoising prior, improving denoising in heavily noisy areas. 2) Formulate event denoising as the upper-level problem in a bilevel optimization, constrained by the lower-level enhancement objective, enabling cross-task interaction so the event representation is learned specifically for the enhancement task rather than as a static pre-processing step.

Result: On the real-world SDE dataset, BiEvLight surpasses SOTA with average improvements of +1.30 dB PSNR, +2.03 dB PSNR*, and +0.047 SSIM. Code: https://github.com/iijjlk/BiEvlight.

Conclusion: Task-aware, bilevel coupling of event denoising and image enhancement—augmented with an image–event gradient prior—reduces noise coupling, avoids the over/under-denoising trade-off of static preprocessing, and materially improves low-light enhancement quality over existing fusion-based methods.

Abstract: Event cameras, with their high dynamic range, show great promise for Low-light Image Enhancement (LLIE). Existing works primarily focus on designing effective modal fusion strategies. However, a key challenge is the dual degradation from intrinsic background activity (BA) noise in events and low signal-to-noise ratio (SNR) in images, which causes severe noise coupling during modal fusion, creating a critical performance bottleneck. We therefore posit that precise event denoising is the prerequisite to unlocking the full potential of event-based fusion. To this end, we propose BiEvLight, a hierarchical and task-aware framework that collaboratively optimizes enhancement and denoising by exploiting their intrinsic interdependence. Specifically, BiEvLight exploits the strong gradient correlation between images and events to build a gradient-guided event denoising prior that alleviates insufficient denoising in heavily noisy regions. Moreover, instead of treating event denoising as a static pre-processing stage-which inevitably incurs a trade-off between over- and under-denoising and cannot adapt to the requirements of a specific enhancement objective-we recast it as a bilevel optimization problem constrained by the enhancement task. Through cross-task interaction, the upper-level denoising problem learns event representations tailored to the lower-level enhancement objective, thereby substantially improving overall enhancement quality. Extensive experiments on the Real-world noise Dataset SDE demonstrate that our method significantly outperforms state-of-the-art (SOTA) approaches, with average improvements of 1.30dB in PSNR, 2.03dB in PSNR* and 0.047 in SSIM, respectively. The code will be publicly available at https://github.com/iijjlk/BiEvlight.

### [48] [3D-RFT: Reinforcement Fine-Tuning for Video-based 3D Scene Understanding](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04976)
*Xiongkun Linghu,Jiangyong Huang,Baoxiong Jia,Siyuan Huang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They introduce 3D-RFT, a reinforcement fine-tuning framework that uses verifiable, task-metric rewards (e.g., 3D IoU, F1) to directly optimize 3D video scene understanding in MLLMs, achieving state-of-the-art results and outperforming larger models.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: SFT with token-level cross-entropy poorly aligns with downstream 3D reasoning metrics, and RL with verifiable rewards has been underused in 3D scene understanding. They aim to close the objective-performance gap by directly optimizing evaluation metrics.

Method: Two-stage pipeline: (1) SFT to initialize a 3D-aware MLLM on video-based 3D tasks; (2) reinforcement fine-tuning via Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) using strictly verifiable, task-specific reward functions derived from metrics like 3D IoU and F1-Score, thereby aligning training with evaluation.

Result: 3D-RFT-4B reaches SOTA across multiple video-based 3D tasks (3D video detection, 3D visual grounding, spatial reasoning) and surpasses larger baselines (e.g., VG LLM-8B). They report robust performance and provide insights on training strategies and data effects.

Conclusion: Direct metric-optimized RL fine-tuning with verifiable rewards is an effective paradigm for video-based 3D scene understanding, offering better alignment and efficiency than SFT, and promising a robust path for future 3D MLLM development.

Abstract: Reinforcement Learning with Verifiable Rewards ( RLVR ) has emerged as a transformative paradigm for enhancing the reasoning capabilities of Large Language Models ( LLMs), yet its potential in 3D scene understanding remains under-explored. Existing approaches largely rely on Supervised Fine-Tuning ( SFT), where the token-level cross-entropy loss acts as an indirect proxy for optimization, leading to a misalignment between training objectives and task performances. To bridge this gap, we present Reinforcement Fine-Tuning for Video-based 3D Scene Understanding (3D-RFT ), the first framework to extend RLVR to video-based 3D perception and reasoning. 3D-RFT shifts the paradigm by directly optimizing the model towards evaluation metrics. 3D-RFT first activates 3D-aware Multi-modal Large Language Models ( MLLM s) via SFT, followed by reinforcement fine-tuning using Group Relative Policy Optimization ( GRPO) with strictly verifiable reward functions. We design task-specific reward functions directly from metrics like 3D IoU and F1-Score to provide more effective signals to guide model training. Extensive experiments demonstrate that 3D-RFT-4B achieves state-of-the-art performance on various video-based 3D scene understanding tasks. Notably, 3D-RFT-4B significantly outperforms larger models (e.g., VG LLM-8B) on 3D video detection, 3D visual grounding, and spatial reasoning benchmarks. We further reveal good properties of 3D-RFT such as robust efficacy, and valuable insights into training strategies and data impact. We hope 3D-RFT can serve as a robust and promising paradigm for future development of 3D scene understanding.
